<p>A <b>developed country</b>, <b>industrialized country</b>, or "<b>more economically developed country</b>" (<b>MEDC</b>), is a <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">sovereign state</a> that has a highly developed economy and advanced technological infrastructure relative to other less industrialized nations. Most commonly, the criteria for evaluating the degree of economic development are <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">gross domestic product</a> (GDP), <a href="/wiki/Gross_national_product" title="Gross national product">gross national product</a> (GNP), the <a href="/wiki/Per_capita_income" title="Per capita income">per capita income</a>, level of industrialization, amount of widespread infrastructure and general standard of living.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> Which criteria are to be used and which countries can be classified as being developed are subjects of debate.</p>
<p>Developed countries have <a href="/wiki/Post-industrial_society" title="Post-industrial society">post-industrial</a> economies, meaning the <a href="/wiki/Service_sector" class="mw-redirect" title="Service sector">service sector</a> provides more wealth than the <a href="/wiki/Industrial_sector" class="mw-redirect" title="Industrial sector">industrial sector</a>. They are contrasted with <a href="/wiki/Developing_country" title="Developing country">developing countries</a>, which are in the process of <a href="/wiki/Industrialization" class="mw-redirect" title="Industrialization">industrialization</a>, or undeveloped countries, which are pre-industrial and almost entirely <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">agrarian</a>. As of 2015, advanced economies comprise 60.8% of global GDP based on <a href="/wiki/Nominal_value" class="mw-redirect" title="Nominal value">nominal values</a> and 42.9% of global GDP based on <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">purchasing-power parity</a> (PPP) according to the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> In 2015, the ten largest advanced economies by GDP in both nominal and PPP terms were <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Similar_terms">Similar terms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Developed_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Similar terms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/North%E2%80%93South_divide" title="North–South divide">North–South divide</a></div>
<p>Terms similar to <i>developed country</i> include "advanced country", "industrialized country", "'more developed country" (MDC), "more economically developed country" (MEDC), "Global North country", "first world country", and "post-industrial country". The term industrialized country may be somewhat ambiguous, as <a href="/wiki/Industrialization" class="mw-redirect" title="Industrialization">industrialization</a> is an ongoing process that is hard to define. The first industrialized country was the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, followed by Belgium. Later it spread further to <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> and other <a href="/wiki/Western_Europe" title="Western Europe">Western European</a> countries. According to some <a href="/wiki/Economist" title="Economist">economists</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Jeffrey_Sachs" title="Jeffrey Sachs">Jeffrey Sachs</a>, however, the current divide between the developed and developing world is largely a phenomenon of the 20th century.<sup id="cite_ref-The_End_of_Poverty_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_End_of_Poverty-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Definition_and_criteria">Definition and criteria</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Developed_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Definition and criteria">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Economic criteria have tended to dominate discussions. One such criterion is income per capita; countries with high <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">gross domestic product</a> (GDP) per capita would thus be described as developed countries. Another economic criterion is <a href="/wiki/Industrialization" class="mw-redirect" title="Industrialization">industrialization</a>; countries in which the <a href="/wiki/Tertiary_sector_of_industry" class="mw-redirect" title="Tertiary sector of industry">tertiary</a> and <a href="/wiki/Quaternary_sector_of_industry" class="mw-redirect" title="Quaternary sector of industry">quaternary sectors of industry</a> dominate would thus be described as developed. More recently another measure, the <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a> (HDI), which combines an economic measure, national income, with other measures, indices for life expectancy and education has become prominent. This criterion would define developed countries as those with a very high (HDI) rating.</p>
<p>According to the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Statistics_Division" title="United Nations Statistics Division">United Nations Statistics Division</a>:</p>
<dl>
<dd>There is no established convention for the designation of "developed" and "developing" countries or areas in the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> system.<sup id="cite_ref-unstated.un.org_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unstated.un.org-5">[5]</a></sup></dd>
</dl>
<p>And it notes that:</p>
<dl>
<dd>The designations "developed" and "developing" are intended for statistical convenience and do not necessarily express a judgement about the stage reached by a particular country or area in the development process.<sup id="cite_ref-unstats.un.org_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unstats.un.org-6">[6]</a></sup></dd>
</dl>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_Development_Index_.28HDI.29">Human Development Index (HDI)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Developed_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Human Development Index (HDI)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_Human_Development_Index" title="List of countries by Human Development Index">List of countries by Human Development Index</a></div>
<p>The UN HDI is a statistical measure that gauges a country's level of human development. While there is a strong correlation between having a high HDI score and a prosperous economy, the UN points out that the HDI accounts for more than income or productivity. Unlike GDP per capita or per capita income, the HDI takes into account how income is turned "into education and health opportunities and therefore into higher levels of human development."</p>
<p>Since 1990, <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a> (2001–2006, 2009–2013), <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a> (1990–1991 and 1993), <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a> (1992 and 1994–2000) and <a href="/wiki/Iceland" title="Iceland">Iceland</a> (2007–2008) have had the highest HDI score. The top 47 countries have scores ranging from 0.793 in <a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">Barbados</a> to 0.955 in <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a>.</p>
<p>Many countries listed by IMF or<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[Note 1]</a></sup> CIA as "advanced" (as of 2009), possess an HDI over 0.788 (as of 2010). Many countries<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[Note 2]</a></sup> possessing an HDI of 0.788 and over (as of 2010) are also listed by IMF or CIA as "advanced" (as of 2009). Thus, many "advanced economies" (as of 2009) are characterized by an HDI score of 0.9 or higher (as of 2007). Since April 2016, the IMF classifies Macau as an advanced economy.<sup id="cite_ref-qq_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-qq-9">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>The latest index was released on 14 December 2015 and covers the period up to 2014. The following are the 49 countries in the top <a href="/wiki/Quartile" title="Quartile">quartile</a> - having an HDI above 0.8, and classified as possessing a "Very high human development".</p>
<ul>
<li><img alt="Increase" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/11px-Increase2.svg.png" title="Increase" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/17px-Increase2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/22px-Increase2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300" /> = Increase</li>
<li><img alt="Steady" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/11px-Steady2.svg.png" title="Steady" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/17px-Steady2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/22px-Steady2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300" /> = No increase or decrease</li>
<li><img alt="Decrease" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/11px-Decrease2.svg.png" title="Decrease" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/17px-Decrease2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/22px-Decrease2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300" /> = Decrease</li>
<li>The number in parentheses represents the number of ranks the country has climbed (up or down) relative to the ranking in 2014 report.</li>
</ul>

</div>
<p>As a non-UN member, the government of <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a> calculates its own HDI, which had a value of 0.882 in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[9]</a></sup> Additionally, while the HDI for the Chinese <a href="/wiki/Special_administrative_region" class="mw-redirect" title="Special administrative region">special administrative region</a> of Hong Kong is calculated by the UN, it is not for <a href="/wiki/Macau" title="Macau">Macau</a>. The Macanese government calculated the territory's HDI to be 0.868 in 2011. These values place both Taiwan and Macau well within the list of countries with "Very high human development".<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[10]</a></sup> Furthermore, in 2009 a United Nations project calculated the HDI for all of its members, as well as Taiwan, Macau, and many <a href="/wiki/Dependent_territory" title="Dependent territory">dependent territories</a>. The HDI values for the countries of <a href="/wiki/San_Marino" title="San Marino">San Marino</a> and <a href="/wiki/Monaco" title="Monaco">Monaco</a>, which have not been included in official annual HDI reports, were found to be at 0.961 and 0.956 respectively. This places both countries firmly within the category of countries with "Very high human development" as well. The dependent territories with HDI values equivalent to "Very high human development" were: <a href="/wiki/Jersey" title="Jersey">Jersey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cayman_Islands" title="Cayman Islands">Cayman Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bermuda" title="Bermuda">Bermuda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guernsey" title="Guernsey">Guernsey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar" title="Gibraltar">Gibraltar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Norfolk_Island" title="Norfolk Island">Norfolk Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/Faroe_Islands" title="Faroe Islands">Faroe Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Man" title="Isle of Man">Isle of Man</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_Virgin_Islands" title="British Virgin Islands">British Virgin Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Falkland_Islands" title="Falkland Islands">Falkland Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aruba" title="Aruba">Aruba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a>, <a href="/wiki/Martinique" title="Martinique">Martinique</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greenland" title="Greenland">Greenland</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Guam" title="Guam">Guam</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-UN_Escap_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_Escap-13">[11]</a></sup> Of note, the HDI values in the 2009 report were calculated using the old HDI formula, while HDI values after the year 2010 are calculated with a different formula.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Net_take-home_pay_of_OECD_members">Net take-home pay of OECD members</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Developed_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Net take-home pay of OECD members">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_net_take-home_pay" title="List of countries by net take-home pay">List of countries by net take-home pay</a></div>
<p>While <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)_per_capita" title="List of countries by GDP (PPP) per capita">GDP per capita</a> is often used to measure how developed a country is, it includes components that do not contribute to a citizen's standard of living. GDP per capita may increase while real incomes for the majority decline. However, measuring only <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_net_take-home_pay" title="List of countries by net take-home pay">net take-home pay</a> gives a more accurate picture of a country's standard of living. The tables show net income figures published annually in the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_for_Economic_Co-operation_and_Development" title="Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development">OECD</a> Tax Database.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[12]</a></sup> They reflect the annual augmented total net take-home pay, by family-type, deducting taxes and non-tax compulsory payments. Since <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">PPP</a> conversion is a widely accepted way to compare income, the OECD publishes the data in USD PPPs. The two major family-types, married with two children and single with no child at 100% average wage have been selected to give an accurate picture of the wage levels.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Gallup_median_household_and_per-capita_income">Gallup median household and per-capita income</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Developed_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Gallup median household and per-capita income">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In 2013, <a href="/wiki/Gallup_(company)" title="Gallup (company)">Gallup</a> published a list of countries with median per capita and <a href="/wiki/Household_income" title="Household income">household income</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-gallup.com_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gallup.com-16">[14]</a></sup> Using <a href="/wiki/Median" title="Median">median</a>, rather than <a href="/wiki/Mean" title="Mean">mean</a> income, results in a much more accurate picture of the average income of the <a href="/wiki/Middle_class" title="Middle class">middle class</a> since the data will not be skewed by gains and abnormalities in the extreme ends. The figures are in <a href="/wiki/International_dollars" class="mw-redirect" title="International dollars">international dollars</a> using <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">purchasing power parity</a> and are based on responses from at least 2,000 adults in each country, with the data aggregated from 2006 to 2012. Below is a list of the top 30 countries in each category.</p>
<div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_lists_of_developed_countries">Other lists of developed countries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Developed_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Other lists of developed countries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Some institutions have produced lists of developed countries: the UN (list shown above), the CIA,<sup id="cite_ref-cia_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-17">[15]</a></sup> and some providers of stock market indices(the <a href="/wiki/FTSE_Group" title="FTSE Group">FTSE Group</a>, <a href="/wiki/MSCI" title="MSCI">MSCI</a>, <a href="/wiki/S%26P" class="mw-redirect" title="S&amp;P">S&amp;P</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dow_Jones" class="mw-redirect" title="Dow Jones">Dow Jones</a>, <a href="/wiki/STOXX" title="STOXX">STOXX</a>, etc.). The latter is not included here because its association of developed countries with countries with both high incomes and <a href="/wiki/Developed_market" title="Developed market">developed markets</a> is not deemed as directly relevant.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="(May 2015)">why?</span></a></i>]</sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[Note 3]</a></sup></p>
<p>However many other institutions have created more general lists referred to when discussing developed countries. For example, the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a> (IMF) identifies 39 "advanced economies".<sup id="cite_ref-qq_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-qq-9">[7]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sanmarino_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sanmarino-19">[16]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Organisation_for_Economic_Co-operation_and_Development" title="Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development">OECD</a>'s 35 members are known as the "developed countries club"<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[17]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[18]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[19]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> identifies 79 "high income countries".<sup id="cite_ref-wb_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wb-23">[20]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="World_Bank_high-income_economies">World Bank high-income economies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Developed_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: World Bank high-income economies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:High_income_country_economies_by_world_bank_2015.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/High_income_country_economies_by_world_bank_2015.png/300px-High_income_country_economies_by_world_bank_2015.png" width="300" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/High_income_country_economies_by_world_bank_2015.png/450px-High_income_country_economies_by_world_bank_2015.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/High_income_country_economies_by_world_bank_2015.png/600px-High_income_country_economies_by_world_bank_2015.png 2x" data-file-width="2753" data-file-height="1400" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:High_income_country_economies_by_world_bank_2015.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/World_Bank_high-income_economy" title="World Bank high-income economy">World Bank high-income economy</a> map</div>

<p>According to the World Bank the following 79 countries (including territories) are classified as "high-income economies".<sup id="cite_ref-wb_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wb-23">[20]</a></sup> In parentheses are the year(s) during which they held such classification since classification began in 1987.<sup id="cite_ref-worldbank1_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worldbank1-24">[21]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="IMF_advanced_economies">IMF advanced economies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Developed_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: IMF advanced economies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:IMF_advanced_economies_2008.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/IMF_advanced_economies_2008.svg/300px-IMF_advanced_economies_2008.svg.png" width="300" height="152" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/IMF_advanced_economies_2008.svg/450px-IMF_advanced_economies_2008.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/IMF_advanced_economies_2008.svg/600px-IMF_advanced_economies_2008.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="940" data-file-height="477" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:IMF_advanced_economies_2008.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #0000FF; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Countries described as Advanced Economies by the IMF</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>According to the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a>, the following 39 economies are classified as "advanced economies":<sup id="cite_ref-qq_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-qq-9">[7]</a></sup></p>
<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 18em; -webkit-column-width: 18em; column-width: 18em;">

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="High-income_OECD_members">High-income OECD members</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Developed_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: High-income OECD members">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>There are 33 members in the High-income OECD category, as determined by the World Bank.<sup id="cite_ref-HighOECD_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HighOECD-25">[22]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-OECD_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OECD-26">[23]</a></sup> The High-income OECD membership is as follows:</p>
<p>25 countries in <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>:</p>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Development_Assistance_Committee_members">Development Assistance Committee members</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Developed_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Development Assistance Committee members">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:DAC_members.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/DAC_members.svg/300px-DAC_members.svg.png" width="300" height="154" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/DAC_members.svg/450px-DAC_members.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/DAC_members.svg/600px-DAC_members.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="863" data-file-height="443" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:DAC_members.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Member nations of the <a href="/wiki/Development_Assistance_Committee" title="Development Assistance Committee">Development Assistance Committee</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>There are 30&#160;members—29 selected <a href="/wiki/Organisation_for_Economic_Co-operation_and_Development" title="Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development">OECD</a> member countries and the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>—in the <a href="/wiki/Development_Assistance_Committee" title="Development Assistance Committee">Development Assistance Committee</a> (DAC),<sup id="cite_ref-DAC_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DAC-27">[24]</a></sup> a group of the world's major donor countries that discuss issues surrounding <a href="/wiki/Development_aid" title="Development aid">development aid</a> and <a href="/wiki/Poverty_reduction" title="Poverty reduction">poverty reduction</a> in <a href="/wiki/Developing_country" title="Developing country">developing countries</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-dac_dat_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dac_dat-28">[25]</a></sup> The following OECD member countries are DAC members:</p>
<p>23 countries wholly or partly in <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>:</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Paris_Club_members">Paris Club members</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Developed_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Paris Club members">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:427px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Map_of_Paris_Club.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Map_of_Paris_Club.png/425px-Map_of_Paris_Club.png" width="425" height="187" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Map_of_Paris_Club.png/638px-Map_of_Paris_Club.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Map_of_Paris_Club.png/850px-Map_of_Paris_Club.png 2x" data-file-width="1427" data-file-height="628" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Map_of_Paris_Club.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Permanent members of the <a href="/wiki/Paris_Club" title="Paris Club">Paris Club</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>There are 22 permanent members in the <a href="/wiki/Paris_Club" title="Paris Club">Paris Club</a> (<a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <span lang="fr" xml:lang="fr"><i><b>Club de Paris</b></i></span>), a group of officials from major creditor countries whose role is to find coordinated and sustainable solutions to the payment difficulties experienced by debtor countries.</p>
<p>15 countries wholly or partly in <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>:</p>
<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 18em; -webkit-column-width: 18em; column-width: 18em;">

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Developed_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-7"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-7">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The official classification of "advanced economies" is originally made by the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a> (IMF). The IMF list doesn't deal with non-IMF members. The <a href="/wiki/Central_Intelligence_Agency" title="Central Intelligence Agency">Central Intelligence Agency</a> (CIA) intends to follow IMF list but adds few economies which aren't dealt with by IMF due to their not being IMF members. By May 2001, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.cia.gov/library/publications/the-world-factbook/appendix/appendix-b.html">the advanced country list of the CIA</a> was more comprehensive than the original IMF list. However, since May 2001, three additional countries (<a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Cyprus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">Malta</a> and <a href="/wiki/Slovenia" title="Slovenia">Slovenia</a>) have been added to the original IMF list, thus leaving the CIA list not updated.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-8"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-8">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Namely sovereign states, i.e., excluding <a href="/wiki/Macau" title="Macau">Macau</a>: In 2003, the government of Macau calculated its HDI as being 0.909 (the UN does not calculate Macau's HDI); In January 2007, the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://english.people.com.cn/200701/29/eng20070129_345749.html">People's Daily</a> reported (from <i>China Modernization Report 2007</i>): "In 2004... Macau... had reached the level of developed countries". The <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.unctad.org/en/docs/tdstat30_enfr.pdf">UNCTAD</a> organisation (of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">UN</a>), as well as the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.cia.gov/library/publications/the-world-factbook/appendix/appendix-b.html">CIA</a>, classify Macau as a "developing" territory. The <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://web.worldbank.org/servlets/ECR?contentMDK=20421402&amp;sitePK=239419#High_income">World Bank</a> classifies Macau as a high income economy (along with developed economies as well as with few developing economies).</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-18"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-18">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.ftse.com/products/downloads/FTSE-Country-Classification-Update_latest.pdf">The Developed Countries Glossary</a> entry reads: "The following countries are classified by FTSE as developed countries: Australia, Austria, Belgium/Luxembourg, Canada, Denmark, Finland, France, Germany, Greece, Hong Kong (People's Republic of China), Ireland, Israel, Italy, Japan, Netherlands, New Zealand, Norway, Portugal, Singapore, South Korea, Spain, Sweden, Switzerland, United Kingdom and the United States."</span></li>
</ol>
</div>

<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;">
<ol class="references">
